    Apr 8, 2010 08:20 PM UTC by marco@.... 
    Hi Jeff,
looking at your connection list (netstat) I have 2 questions:

1 How do you submit the jobs?
Using condor-g with the condor grid monitor enabled should reduce the
number of connections.
http://www.cs.wisc.edu/condor/manual/v7.4/5_3Grid_Universe.html#SECTION00632600000000000000
https://twiki.grid.iu.edu/bin/view/Troubleshooting/GridMonitor

2 Most of the connections are in TIME_WAIT. Which is your TCP timeout?
You can see it in
/proc/sys/net/ipv4/tcp_fin_timeout
The linux default is 60 (seconds). Specially if the
submissions/connections are local you can decrease that and allow quicker
reuse of the ports.
Too short timeout could cause problems (packets from old connections
closing new ones on the same port)
Can you see what is happening if you put that to 20?

Cheers,
Marco

4.  We **may** be getting a new production cluster in the same timeframe as the move - it is expected that our current production cluster will become dedicated to OSG use.  In which case, it will get a fresh install for all OS's and OSG stack - Alain, this is what I referenced when I asked weeks ago about 64-bit system compatibility with the OSG stack. If this does in fact happen in the July time frame, then two cases are possible.  Case 1:  If the problem is gone - all is good.  Case 2:  If the problem persists, it will then be on different OS versions and OSG stack version in which case a new GOC ticket can be started with what will be fresh debugging info.

Any thoughts on this?

    Yeah, you're showing all of the open files--you can use it to show all the open network connections. I think it's "lsof -i TCP". At least, that's what I use. It's only useful as "root" though, not as another user.

Kyle
    Feb 11, 2010 03:56 PM UTC by Jeffrey Dutton 
    A quick update.

Here are the changes that have been made to date and the impact the change has had on this issue (if known):

0.  The firewall on the CE was disabled - this is the only way jobs run consistently and this is really unacceptable.

1.  The PBS server(cluster headnode) andht eCE were both made NIS slaves - this has stopped the whoami call failures completely

2.  To further reduce any network call latency, the PBS sever and CE were configured as caching-nameservers and the network service caching daemon was started.  No known impact other than there seems to be no more GRAM 47 errors at all when submitting lots of jobs.

3.  Enabling the firewall on the CE after these changes causes GRAM 12 errors to show up almost immediately and jobs fail to be submitted.

4.  With the firewall off on the CE, submitting 3x the number of job slots on the site causes many problems (GRAM 10 errors) once the jobs start going into the queue.  At one point I was able to get as many as 109 jobs in queue but that was the maximum.  The process of job submission seems to slow dramatically.

5.  Submitting just under the number of job slots (say 55 jobs with 58 slots available) is very consistent in that all jobs will submit successfully.  In fact, it has been pretty consistent for up to 5 jobs in queue but then the failures begin and they progressively get worse the more jobs put into queue.

6.  I have new hardware on order and anticipate I will be able to build a new CE in the future.  Should a clean OS install and a fresh OSG CE install resolve the issue, the CE will be swapped with the later build.

If there are ways to progress in resolving this issue, I am out of ideas.  I am open to suggestions at this point.

Thanks!

Jeff
    Feb 8, 2010 04:29 PM UTC by Jeffrey Dutton 
    Hello,

A quick update.

Following Alain's advice and not doing a complete reinstallation for fear of spending a lot of time reproducing the error, I have done a lot of testing and some modifications to the site.

0.  The firewall on the CE was lowered - this will be rectified once the following changes below are finished.

1. We observed times when logging in as different users on OSG servers had a significant variation in the time to a successful login - and many user login failures when the CE was busy.

Action Taken #1:  Created two new NIS slaves - one on the cluster headnode (PBS server) and one on the CE.  More testing is needed but a "whoami" call failure has not been seen since.  The reason for the cluster NIS slave is to improve latency in NIS related calls from the compute nodes without having to hit our primary NIS server, which they had been doing.

Action Taken #2:  To further reduce NIS timeouts and delays, the nscd daemon was started (and will restart at boot) on all OSG servers and the cluster headnode (PBS server)

2. In our production cluster, DNS calls were also an issue, considering our architecture, and seemed to induce problems with PBS.

Action TO BE TAKEN:  We will be making our cluster headnode a caching-nameserver to reduce DNS call latency.

3. To be done:  Re-enable the firewall on the CE and test.

This is it for now.

    Jan 15, 2010 05:30 PM UTC by Jeffrey Dutton 
    /etc/xinetd.d/globus-gatekeeper looks like this:

[root@vdgateway xinetd.d]# cat globus-gatekeeper
# Note: This file is managed by vdt-control.  You can edit this file,
# but to avoid having your changes overwritten by vdt-control, edit
# /opt/osg-1.2/vdt/services/xinetd-globus-gatekeeper
# and reset it with "vdt-control --on"
service globus-gatekeeper
{
socket_type = stream
protocol    = tcp
wait        = no
user        = root
instances   = UNLIMITED
cps         = 400 10
per_source  = 300
server      = /opt/osg-1.2/vdt/services/vdt-run-globus-gatekeeper.sh
disable     = no
}

    Jan 13, 2010 11:06 PM UTC by Jeffrey Dutton 
    Hello,

Having continued my work on this problem I have found the following concerning iptables and necessary port openings for the OSG stack to work from the release documentation Firewall Document.

First, I know that tcp port 2119 needs to be open.

Here is the relevant line in my iptables list:

-A RH-Firewall-1-INPUT -m state --state NEW -m tcp -p tcp --dport 2119 -j ACCEPT

However, when I enable iptables logging, I see **lots** of blocks such as this:

Jan 13 17:06:37 vdgateway kernel: '***BLOCKED-2***'IN=eth0 OUT= MAC=00:30:48:98:e5:d6:00:30:48:8e:95:16:08:00 SRC=155.37.255.131 DST=155.37.255.141 LEN=40 TOS=0x00 PREC=0x00 TTL=64 ID=0 DF PROTO=TCP SPT=40003 DPT=2119 WINDOW=0 RES=0x00 RST URGP=0

Now 155.37.255.131 is the client (vdtclient1.vcell.uchc.edu) and 155.37.255.141 is the CE (vdgateway.vcell.uchc.edu) that the client submits OSG jobs to.

While I can't exactly match these blocks to Gram 12 errors, enough have occurred concurrently to make me suspicious (tail -f on /var/log/messages watching for blocks and seeing GRAM 12 errors on the client side happening at the same time).

I have not seen anything like this before.  Has anyone seen this behavior before that may have a workaround?  I have and will continue looking for a solution on the web.

I don't think it is blocking all the time else I would not get a single job to run.  It seems intermittent and that is what makes it even more strange.
